NAME OF DATA SET: 
Northern Hemisphere Tree-Ring-Based STD and RCS Temperature Reconstructions

of underlying raw tree ring data.  12/2009 - Addition of Gulf of Alaska 
regional reconstruction. Original receipt by WDC Paleo 10/2006, 
hemispheric reconstruction only. 

CONTRIBUTORS: Rosanne D'Arrigo and Gordon Jacoby, 
Lamont-Doherty Earth Observatory, and Rob Wilson, University of Edinburgh.
IGBP PAGES/WDCA CONTRIBUTION SERIES NUMBER: 2006-092

SUGGESTED DATA CITATION: D'Arrigo, R., et al. 2006. 
Northern Hemisphere Tree-Ring-Based STD and RCS Temperature Reconstructions.
IGBP PAGES/World Data Center for Paleoclimatology

ORIGINAL REFERENCE: 
D'Arrigo, R., R. Wilson, and G. Jacoby.  2006.
On the long-term context for late twentieth century warming. 
Journal of Geophysical Research, 111, D03103, doi:10.1029/2005JD006352.

ABSTRACT:
Previous tree-ring–based Northern Hemisphere temperature reconstructions 
portray a varying amplitude range between the "Medieval Warm Period"(MWP), 
"Little Ice Age" (LIA) and present. We describe a new reconstruction, 
developed using largely different methodologies and additional new data 
compared to previous efforts. Unlike earlier studies, we quantify differences 
between more traditional (STD) and Regional Curve Standardization (RCS) 
methodologies, concluding that RCS is superior for retention of low-frequency 
trends. Continental North American versus Eurasian RCS series developed 
prior to merging to the hemispheric scale cohere surprisingly well, 
suggesting common forcing, although there are notable deviations 
(e.g., fifteenth to sixteenth century). Results indicate clear MWP (warm), 
LIA (cool), and recent (warm) episodes. Direct interpretation of the RCS 
reconstruction suggests that MWP temperatures were nearly 0.7C cooler than 
in the late twentieth century, with an amplitude difference of 1.14C from 
the coldest (1600–1609) to warmest (1937-1946) decades. However, we advise 
caution with this analysis. Although we conclude, as found elsewhere, that 
recent warming has been substantial relative to natural fluctuations of the 
past millennium, we also note that owing to the spatially heterogeneous 
nature of the MWP, and its different timing within different regions, 
present palaeoclimatic methodologies will likely "flatten out" estimates 
for this period relative to twentieth century warming, which expresses 
a more homogenous global "fingerprint." Therefore we stress that presently 
available paleoclimatic reconstructions are inadequate for making specific 
inferences, at hemispheric scales, about MWP warmth relative to the present 
anthropogenic period and that such comparisons can only still be made at 
the local/regional scale.

GEOGRAPHIC REGION: Northern Hemisphere
PERIOD OF RECORD: 713 - 1995 AD
FUNDING SOURCES: National Science Foundation (USA) Earth System History 
Program and the NOAA (USA) Climate Change and Detection Program.


DESCRIPTION:  
Two new tree-ring-based reconstructions of Northern Hemisphere annual 
temperatures, computed by (1) Standard (STD) negative-exponential or 
straightline curve fits, and by (2) Regional Curve Standardization (RCS).  

The tree-ring network consists of ring width (and limited density) data 
derived from living and subfossil wood of coniferous tree species 
compiled from 66 high elevation and latitudinal treeline North American 
and Eurasian sites. Individual sites, or regional composites (identified 
using principal component analysis) were standardized and merged to 
create regional, continental and hemispheric scale records. The North 
American data include new or extended millennial-length records, and 
updates of most of the data sets until at least the late 1990s.  

The regional reconstruction for the Gulf of Alaska was added to this file 
in December 2009.  This regional series is based on an RCS standardization 
of a composite treering data collection of living and subfossil samples.  
The RCS chronology file is archived in the ITRDB at:
ftp://ftp.ncdc.noaa.gov/pub/data/paleo/treering/chronologies/northamerica/usa/ak096c.crn
The composite tree ring measurements file from which the chronology was computed 
consists of 820 living and subfossil tree ring data series.  The measurements 
are archived in the ITRDB at:
ftp://ftp.ncdc.noaa.gov/pub/data/paleo/treering/measurements/northamerica/usa/ak096.rwl 
This collection is more fully described at:
ftp://ftp.ncdc.noaa.gov/pub/data/paleo/treering/measurements/correlation-stats/ak096.txt 
This regional reconstruction was a component in the Kaufman et al. 2009 
2,000 Year Arctic Temperature Synthesis.  Wilson et al. 2007 produced a Gulf of Alaska 
reconstruction based on an STD chronology derived from the same 820 ringwidth series. 


Composite regional tree ring chronologies for 19 regions used in the study 
were added to this file May 2012.  Both RCS and STD chronologies were added 
for each of the 19 regional composites.  In addition, notes on the raw ringwidth 
data included in each composite were added below: 

Data sources used in D’Arrigo et al. (2006) – DWJ06
D'Arrigo, R., Wilson, R. and Jacoby, G. 2006. 
On the long-term context for late 20th century warming. 
(Journal of Geophysical Research, Vol. 111, D03103, doi:10.1029/2005JD006352

Locations of regional groups and sites are shown in Figure 1, DWJ06. 
Table 1 detailed individual chronology meta data.

2. RCS Gulf of Alaska Regional Temperature Reconstruction
Annual temperature, degrees Celsius 

This regional series is based on an RCS standardization of a composite 
treering data collection of living and subfossil samples in coastal Alaska.  
The RCS chronology file is archived in the ITRDB at:
ftp://ftp.ncdc.noaa.gov/pub/data/paleo/treering/chronologies/northamerica/usa/ak096c.crn
The composite tree ring measurements file from which the chronology was computed 
consists of 820 living and subfossil tree ring data series.  The measurements 
are archived in the ITRDB at:
ftp://ftp.ncdc.noaa.gov/pub/data/paleo/treering/measurements/northamerica/usa/ak096.rwl 
This collection is more fully described at:
ftp://ftp.ncdc.noaa.gov/pub/data/paleo/treering/measurements/correlation-stats/ak096.txt 
This regional reconstruction was a component in the Kaufman et al. 2009 
2,000 Year Arctic Temperature Synthesis.
